id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[121]</a></sup> and 105 <a href="/wiki/Nature_parks_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature parks (Germany)">nature parks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup> More than <a href="/wiki/List_of_zoos_in_Germany" title="List of zoos in Germany">400 zoos and animal parks</a> operate in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Zoological_Garden" title="Berlin Zoological Garden">Berlin Zoo</a>, which opened in 1844, is the oldest in Germany, and claims the most comprehensive collection of species in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Germany" title="Politics of Germany">Politics of Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Germany" title="Taxation in Germany">Taxation in Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Federal_budget_of_Germany" title="Federal budget of Germany">Federal budget of Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable floatright"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Frank-Walter Steinmeier - 2018 (cropped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg/155px-Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="155" height="213" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg/233px-Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg/310px-Frank-Walter_Steinmeier_-_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1749" data-file-height="2398"></a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angela_Merkel_2019_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Angela Merkel 2019 (cropped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Angela_Merkel_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Angela_Merkel_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="213" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Angela_Merkel_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Angela_Merkel_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Angela_Merkel_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Angela_Merkel_2019_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1554" data-file-height="2209"></a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier" title="Frank-Walter Steinmeier">Frank-Walter Steinmeier</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Germany" title="President of Germany">President</a></small> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Chancellor</a></small> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Germany is a <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democratic">parliamentary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic. Federal <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a> is vested in the parliament consisting of the <i><a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a></i> (Federal Diet) and <i><a href="/wiki/Bundesrat_of_Germany" title="Bundesrat of Germany">Bundesrat</a></i> (Federal Council), which together form the legislative body. The <i>Bundestag</i> is elected through <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">direct elections</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Mixed-member_proportional_representation" title="Mixed-member proportional representation">mixed-member proportional representation</a> system. The members of the <i>Bundesrat</i> represent and are appointed by the governments of the sixteen federated states.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> The German political system operates under a framework laid out in the 1949 constitution known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_for_the_Federal_Republic_of_Germany" title="Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany">Grundgesetz</a></i> (Basic Law). Amendments generally require a two-thirds majority of both the <i>Bundestag</i> and the <i>Bundesrat</i>; the fundamental principles of the constitution, as expressed in the articles guaranteeing human dignity, the separation of powers, the federal structure, and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>, are valid in perpetuity.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Germany" title="President of Germany">president</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier" title="Frank-Walter Steinmeier">Frank-Walter Steinmeier</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and invested primarily with representative responsibilities and powers. He is elected by the <i><a href="/wiki/Bundesversammlung_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesversammlung (Germany)">Bundesversammlung</a></i> (federal convention), an institution consisting of the members of the <i>Bundestag</i> and an equal number of state delegates.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> The second-highest official in the <a href="/wiki/German_order_of_precedence" title="German order of precedence">German order of precedence</a> is the <i>Bundestagspräsident</i> (<a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Bundestag" title="President of the Bundestag">president of the <i>Bundestag</i></a>), who is elected by the <i>Bundestag</i> and responsible for overseeing the daily sessions of the body.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[126]</a></sup> The third-highest official and the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the chancellor, who is appointed by the <i>Bundespräsident</i> after being elected by the party or coalition with the most seats in the <i>Bundestag</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> The chancellor, currently <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, is the head of government and exercises <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> through their <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Germany" title="Cabinet of Germany">Cabinet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 1949, the party system has been dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">Christian Democratic Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a>. So far every chancellor has been a member of one of these parties. However, the smaller liberal <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">Free Democratic Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a> have also been junior partners in <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition governments</a>. Since 2007, the left-wing populist party <a href="/wiki/The_Left_(Germany)" title="The Left (Germany)">The Left</a> has been a staple in the German <i>Bundestag</i>, though they have never been part of the federal government. In the <a href="/wiki/2017_German_federal_election" title="2017 German federal election">2017 German federal election</a>, the right-wing populist <a href="/wiki/Alternative_for_Germany" title="Alternative for Germany">Alternative for Germany</a> gained enough votes to attain representation in the parliament for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constituent_states">Constituent states</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">States of Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federalism_in_Germany" title="Federalism in Germany">Federalism in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany is a <a href="/wiki/Federal_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal state">federal state</a> and comprises sixteen <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">constituent states</a> which are collectively referred to as <i>Länder</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-134">[129]</a></sup> Each state has its own constitution,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[130]</a></sup> and is largely autonomous in regard to its internal organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-134">[129]</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Germany is divided into 401 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Germany" title="Districts of Germany">districts</a> (<i>Kreise</i>) at a municipal level; these consist of 294 <a href="/wiki/List_of_rural_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rural districts of Germany">rural districts</a> and 107 <a href="/wiki/Urban_districts_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban districts of Germany">urban districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="float: left;margin:0 2em 0 0;">
       <div style="text-shadow:white 0em 0em 0.4em; font-size:75%">

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Germany" title="Law of Germany">Law of Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Germany" title="Judiciary of Germany">Judiciary of Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Germany" title="Law enforcement in Germany">Law enforcement in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany has a <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law system</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> with some references to <a href="/wiki/Germanic_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic law">Germanic law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[135]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Federal_Constitutional_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Constitutional Court of Germany">Bundesverfassungsgericht</a></i> (Federal Constitutional Court) is the German Supreme Court responsible for constitutional matters, with power of <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review" title="Judicial review">judicial review</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[136]</a></sup> Germany's supreme court system is specialised: for civil and criminal cases, the highest court of appeal is the <a href="/wiki/Inquisitorial_system" title="Inquisitorial system">inquisitorial</a> <a href="/wiki/Federal_Court_of_Justice_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Court of Justice of Germany">Federal Court of Justice</a>, and for other affairs the courts are the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Labor_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Labor Court of Germany">Federal Labour Court</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bundessozialgericht" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundessozialgericht">Federal Social Court</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Finance_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Finance Court of Germany">Federal Finance Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Administrative Court of Germany">Federal Administrative Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[137]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Criminal and private laws are codified on the national level in the <i><a href="/wiki/Strafgesetzbuch" title="Strafgesetzbuch">Strafgesetzbuch</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrgerliches_Gesetzbuch" title="Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch">Bürgerliches Gesetzbuch</a></i> respectively. The German penal system seeks the rehabilitation of the criminal and the protection of the public.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup> Except for petty crimes, which are tried before a single professional judge, and serious <a href="/wiki/Political_crime" title="Political crime">political crimes</a>, all charges are tried before mixed tribunals on which <a href="/wiki/Lay_judge" title="Lay judge">lay judges</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6ffe" class="mw-redirect" title="Schöffe">Schöffen</a></i></i>) sit side by side with professional judges.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany has a low murder rate with 1.18 murders per 100,000 as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[141]</a></sup> In 2018, the overall crime rate fell to its lowest since 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Germany" title="Foreign relations of Germany">Foreign relations of Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg/220px-2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg/330px-2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg/440px-2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2017_G20_Hamburg_summit_leaders_group_photo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Germany hosted the <a href="/wiki/2017_G20_Hamburg_summit" title="2017 G20 Hamburg summit">G20 summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, 7–8 July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[143]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany has a network of 227 diplomatic missions abroad<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[144]</a></sup> and maintains relations with more than 190 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[145]</a></sup> Germany is a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">G8</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>. It has played an influential role in the European Union since its inception and has maintained a <a href="/wiki/Franco-German_cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-German cooperation">strong alliance with France</a> and all neighbouring countries since 1990. Germany promotes the creation of a more unified European political, economic and security apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[148]</a></sup> The governments of Germany and the United States are close political allies.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[149]</a></sup> Cultural ties and economic interests have crafted a bond between the two countries resulting in <a href="/wiki/Atlanticism" title="Atlanticism">Atlanticism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The development policy of Germany is an independent area of foreign policy. It is formulated by the Federal Ministry for Economic Cooperation and Development and carried out by the implementing organisations. The German government sees development policy as a joint responsibility of the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup> It was the world's second-biggest aid donor in 2019 after the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[152]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bundeswehr" title="Bundeswehr">Bundeswehr</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany's military, the <i>Bundeswehr</i>, is organised into the <i><a href="/wiki/German_Army" title="German Army">Heer</a></i> (Army and special forces <a href="/wiki/Kommando_Spezialkr%C3%A4fte" title="Kommando Spezialkräfte">KSK</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/German_Navy" title="German Navy">Marine</a></i> (Navy), <i><a href="/wiki/German_Air_Force" title="German Air Force">Luftwaffe</a></i> (Air Force), <i><a href="/wiki/Joint_Medical_Service_(Germany)" title="Joint Medical Service (Germany)">Zentraler Sanitätsdienst der Bundeswehr</a></i> (Joint Medical Service) and <i><a href="/wiki/Streitkr%C3%A4ftebasis" class="mw-redirect" title="Streitkräftebasis">Streitkräftebasis</a></i> (Joint Support Service) branches. In absolute terms, German military expenditure is the 8th highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[153]</a></sup> In 2018, military spending was at $49.5&nbsp;billion, about 1.2% of the country's GDP, well below the NATO target of 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg/220px-Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg/330px-Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg/440px-Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fregatte_Mecklenburg-Vorpommern_F218.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/German_Navy" title="German Navy">German Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-class_frigate" title="Brandenburg-class frigate">Brandenburg-class frigate</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>As of January&nbsp;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <i>Bundeswehr</i> has a strength of 184,001 active soldiers and 80,947 civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-bundeswehr_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bundeswehr-161">[156]</a></sup> Reservists are available to the armed forces and participate in defence exercises and deployments abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-bwzukunft_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bwzukunft-162">[157]</a></sup> Until 2011, <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Germany" title="Conscription in Germany">military service</a> was compulsory for men at age 18, but this has been officially suspended and replaced with a voluntary service.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[159]</a></sup> Since 2001 women may serve in all functions of service without restriction.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[160]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/SIPRI" class="mw-redirect" title="SIPRI">SIPRI</a>, Germany was the fourth largest exporter of major arms in the world from 2014 to 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In peacetime, the <i>Bundeswehr</i> is commanded by the Minister of Defence. In <a href="/wiki/State_of_Defence_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="State of Defence (Germany)">state of defence</a>, the Chancellor would become commander-in-chief of the <i>Bundeswehr</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[162]</a></sup> The role of the <i>Bundeswehr</i> is described in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of Germany">Constitution of Germany</a> as defensive only. But after a ruling of the Federal Constitutional Court in 1994 the term "defence" has been defined to not only include protection of the borders of Germany, but also crisis reaction and conflict prevention, or more broadly as guarding the <a href="/wiki/Security" title="Security">security</a> of Germany anywhere in the world. As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the German military has about 3,600 troops stationed in foreign countries as part of international peacekeeping forces, including about 1,200 supporting operations against <a href="/wiki/Daesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Daesh">Daesh</a>, 980 in the NATO-led <a href="/wiki/Resolute_Support_Mission" title="Resolute Support Mission">Resolute Support Mission</a> in Afghanistan, and 800 in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[164]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Germany" title="Economy of Germany">Economy of Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Germany" title="Science and technology in Germany">Science and technology in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg/220px-Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg/330px-Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg/440px-Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8003" data-file-height="5622"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Skyline_Frankfurt_am_Main_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> is a leading business centre in Europe and the seat of the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-frankfurt_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frankfurt-170">[165]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany has a <a href="/wiki/Social_market_economy" title="Social market economy">social market economy</a> with a highly skilled <a href="/wiki/Labour_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour force">labour force</a>, a low level of corruption, and a high level of <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[167]</a></sup> It is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">third largest exporter</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports" title="List of countries by imports">third largest importer</a> of goods,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_in_Europe_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (nominal)">largest economy in Europe</a>, which is also the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">fourth-largest economy by nominal GDP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wbpdf_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wbpdf-173">[168]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">fifth-largest by PPP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup> Its GDP per capita measured in purchasing power standards amounts to 121% of the EU27 average (100%).<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tertiary sector of industry">service sector</a> contributes approximately 69% of the total GDP, industry 31%, and agriculture 1% as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> The unemployment rate published by <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> amounts to 3.2% as of January&nbsp;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, which is the fourth-lowest in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-176">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany is part of the <a href="/wiki/Internal_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal market">European single market</a> which represents more than 450 million consumers.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[172]</a></sup> In 2017, the country accounted for 28% of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> economy according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-imf.org_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf.org-178">[173]</a></sup> Germany introduced the common European currency, the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a>, in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-euroc_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euroc-179">[174]</a></sup> Its monetary policy is set by the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, which is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-frankfurt_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frankfurt-170">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Being home to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_automobile#19th_century" title="History of the automobile">modern car</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Germany" title="Automotive industry in Germany">automotive industry in Germany</a> is regarded as one of the most competitive and innovative in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[176]</a></sup> and is <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_motor_vehicle_production" title="List of countries by motor vehicle production">the fourth largest by production</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[177]</a></sup> The top 10 exports of Germany are vehicles, machinery, chemical goods, electronic products, electrical equipments, pharmaceuticals, transport equipments, basic metals, food products, and rubber and plastics.<sup id="cite_ref-Destatis_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Destatis-183">[178]</a></sup> Germany is <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">one of the largest exporters globally</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[179]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Of the world's 500 largest stock-market-listed companies measured by revenue in 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a>, 29 are headquartered in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[180]</a></sup> 30 major Germany-based companies are included in the <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a>, the German stock market index which is operated by <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[181]</a></sup> Well-known international brands include <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Telekom" title="Deutsche Telekom">Deutsche Telekom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[182]</a></sup> Berlin is a <a href="/wiki/Startup_ecosystem" title="Startup ecosystem">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup companies</a> and has become the leading location for venture capital funded firms in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[183]</a></sup> Germany is recognised for its large portion of specialised <a href="/wiki/Small_and_medium_enterprises" class="mw-redirect" title="Small and medium enterprises">small and medium enterprises</a>, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Mittelstand" title="Mittelstand">Mittelstand</a></i> model.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[184]</a></sup> These companies represent 48% global market leaders in their segments, labelled <a href="/wiki/Hidden_Champions" class="mw-redirect" title="Hidden Champions">Hidden Champions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">Research and development</a> efforts form an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Germany" title="Economy of Germany">German economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[186]</a></sup> In 2018 Germany ranked fourth globally in terms of number of science and engineering research papers published.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[187]</a></sup> Research institutions in Germany include the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Helmholtz_Association_of_German_Research_Centres" class="mw-redirect" title="Helmholtz Association of German Research Centres">Helmholtz Association</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Society</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Leibniz_Association" title="Leibniz Association">Leibniz Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[188]</a></sup> Germany is the largest contributor to the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[189]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Germany" title="Transport in Germany">Transport in Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Germany" title="Energy in Germany">Energy in Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Germany" title="Telecommunications in Germany">Telecommunications in Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Germany" title="Water supply and sanitation in Germany">Water supply and sanitation in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg/220px-ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg/330px-ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg/440px-ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ICE_3_Oberhaider-Wald-Tunnel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/ICE_3" title="ICE 3">ICE 3</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Cologne%E2%80%93Frankfurt_high-speed_rail_line" title="Cologne–Frankfurt high-speed rail line">Cologne–Frankfurt high-speed rail line</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With its central position in Europe, Germany is a transport hub for the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[190]</a></sup> Its road network is among the densest in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[191]</a></sup> The motorway (<a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a>) is widely known for having no federally mandated <a href="/wiki/Speed_limit" title="Speed limit">speed limit</a> for some classes of vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-wa_16-09-2013_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wa_16-09-2013-197">[192]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">InterCityExpress</a> or <i>ICE</i> train network serves major German cities as well as destinations in neighbouring countries with speeds up to 300&nbsp;km/h (190&nbsp;mph).<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[193]</a></sup> The largest German airports are <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[194]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Hamburg" title="Port of Hamburg">Port of Hamburg</a> is one of the top twenty <a href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_container_ports" class="mw-redirect" title="List of world's busiest container ports">largest container ports in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Germany was the world's seventh-largest consumer of energy.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[196]</a></sup> The government and the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Germany" title="Nuclear power in Germany">nuclear power industry</a> agreed to phase out all <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear power plants</a> by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[197]</a></sup> It meets the country's power demands using 40% <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable sources</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[198]</a></sup> Germany is committed to the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> and several other treaties promoting biodiversity, low emission standards, and <a href="/wiki/Water_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Water management">water management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[201]</a></sup> The country's household recycling rate is among the highest in the world—at around 65%.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[202]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_greenhouse_gas_emissions_per_person" title="List of countries by greenhouse gas emissions per person">greenhouse gas emissions per capita</a> were the ninth highest in the EU in 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[203]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy transition in Germany">German energy transition</a> (<i>Energiewende</i>) is the recognised move to a sustainable economy by means of energy efficiency and renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[204]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Germany" title="Tourism in Germany">Tourism in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg/220px-Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg/330px-Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg/440px-Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2970" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Neuschwanstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Neuschwanstein_Castle" title="Neuschwanstein Castle">Neuschwanstein Castle</a> in Bavaria
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany is the ninth most visited country in the world as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, with 37.4 million visits.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[205]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> has become the third most visited city destination in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[206]</a></sup> Domestic and international travel and tourism combined directly contribute over €105.3&nbsp;billion to German GDP. Including indirect and induced impacts, the industry supports 4.2 million jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[207]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany's most visited and popular landmarks include <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dresden_Frauenkirche" title="Dresden Frauenkirche">Dresden Frauenkirche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuschwanstein_Castle" title="Neuschwanstein Castle">Neuschwanstein Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_Castle" title="Heidelberg Castle">Heidelberg Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wartburg" title="Wartburg">Wartburg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sanssouci_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanssouci Palace">Sanssouci Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[208]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Europa-Park" title="Europa-Park">Europa-Park</a> near <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_im_Breisgau" title="Freiburg im Breisgau">Freiburg</a> is Europe's second most popular theme park resort.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[209]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Germany" title="Demographics of Germany">Demographics of Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>
      </div> 
      <p>With a population of 80.2&nbsp;million according to the 2011 census,<sup id="cite_ref-File_2013_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-File_2013-215">[210]</a></sup> rising to 83.1&nbsp;million as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-2018pop_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018pop-10">[6]</a></sup> Germany is the most populous country in the European Union, the second-most populous country in Europe after <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">nineteenth-most populous country</a> in the world. Its <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">population density</a> stands at 227 inhabitants per square kilometre (588 per square mile). The overall <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy in Germany</a> at birth is 80.19 years (77.93 years for males and 82.58 years for females).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">fertility rate</a> of 1.41 children born per woman (2011 estimates) is below the replacement rate of 2.1 and is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by fertility rate">lowest fertility rates in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> Since the 1970s, Germany's <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rate</a> has exceeded its <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a>. However, Germany is witnessing increased birth rates and migration rates since the beginning of the 2010s, particularly a rise in the number of well-educated migrants. Germany has the third oldest population in the world, with an average age of 47.4 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Four sizeable groups of people are referred to as "national minorities" because their ancestors have lived in their respective regions for centuries:<sup id="cite_ref-BMI_2010_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMI_2010-216">[211]</a></sup> There is a <a href="/wiki/Danes" title="Danes">Danish</a> minority in the northernmost state of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein" title="Schleswig-Holstein">Schleswig-Holstein</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-BMI_2010_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMI_2010-216">[211]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Sorbs" title="Sorbs">Sorbs</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Slavic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic people">Slavic population</a>, are in the <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Saxony" class="mw-redirect" title="Free State of Saxony">Saxony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sinti" title="Sinti">Sinti</a> live throughout the country; and the <a href="/wiki/Frisians" title="Frisians">Frisians</a> are concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein" title="Schleswig-Holstein">Schleswig-Holstein</a>'s western coast and in the north-western part of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BMI_2010_216-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMI_2010-216">[211]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the United States, Germany is the second most popular <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Germany" title="Immigration to Germany">immigration destination</a> in the world. The majority of migrants live in western Germany, in particular in urban areas. Of the country's residents, 18.6&nbsp;million people (22.5%) were of immigrant or partially immigrant descent in 2016 (including persons descending or partially descending from <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_German" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic German">ethnic German</a> repatriates).<sup id="cite_ref-Destatis1_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Destatis1-217">[212]</a></sup> In 2015, the Population Division of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs" title="United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs">United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs</a> listed Germany as host to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population">second-highest number of international migrants worldwide</a>, about 5% or 12&nbsp;million of all 244&nbsp;million migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[213]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Germany ranks fifth amongst EU countries in terms of the percentage of migrants in the country's population, at 12.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany has a number of large <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Germany" title="List of cities and towns in Germany">cities</a>. There are 11 officially recognised <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_regions_in_Germany" title="Metropolitan regions in Germany">metropolitan regions</a>. The country's largest city is <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, while its largest urban area is the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Demographia_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demographia-220">[215]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Germany" title="Religion in Germany">Religion in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:500px_photo_(70560973).jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/500px_photo_%2870560973%29.jpeg/220px-500px_photo_%2870560973%29.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/500px_photo_%2870560973%29.jpeg/330px-500px_photo_%2870560973%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/500px_photo_%2870560973%29.jpeg/440px-500px_photo_%2870560973%29.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1364"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:500px_photo_(70560973).jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a> is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_German_Census" title="2011 German Census">2011 German Census</a> showed <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> as the largest religion in Germany, with 66.8% identified themselves as Christian, with 3.8% of those not being church members.<sup id="cite_ref-Egeler_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egeler-221">[216]</a></sup> 31.7% declared themselves as <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, including members of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Evangelical Church in Germany</a> (which encompasses <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_and_uniting_churches" title="United and uniting churches">administrative or confessional unions of both traditions</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Free_churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Free churches">free churches</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Evangelische Freikirchen</i>); 31.2% declared themselves as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Germany">Roman Catholics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Orthodox</a> believers constituted 1.3%. According to data from 2016, the Catholic Church and the Evangelical Church claimed 28.5% and 27.5%, respectively, of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Eck16_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eck16-222">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EKD2017_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EKD2017-223">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Germany" title="Islam in Germany">Islam</a> is the second largest religion in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Zensus_2011_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zensus_2011-224">[219]</a></sup> In the 2011 census, 1.9% of the census population (1.52&nbsp;million people) gave their religion as Islam, but this figure is deemed unreliable because a disproportionate number of adherents of this religion (and other religions, such as Judaism) are likely to have made use of their right not to answer the question.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[220]</a></sup> Most of the Muslims are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunnis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alevites" class="mw-redirect" title="Alevites">Alevites</a> from Turkey, but there are a small number of <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shi'ites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyyas</a> and other denominations. Other religions comprise less than one percent of Germany's population.<sup id="cite_ref-Zensus_2011_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zensus_2011-224">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A study in 2018 estimated that 38% of the population are not members of any religious organization or <a href="/wiki/Religious_denomination" title="Religious denomination">denomination</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOWID_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOWID-226">[221]</a></sup> though up to a third may still consider themselves religious. <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Germany" title="Irreligion in Germany">Irreligion in Germany</a> is strongest in the former East Germany, which used to be predominantly Protestant before the enforcement of state atheism, and in major metropolitan areas.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-georgetown1_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-georgetown1-228">[223]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Germany" title="Languages of Germany">Languages of Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <p>German is the official and predominant spoken language in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages-229">[224]</a></sup> It is one of 24 official and working languages of the European Union, and one of the three procedural languages of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[225]</a></sup> German is the most widely spoken first language in the European Union, with around 100 million native speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[226]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recognised native minority languages in Germany are <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low_Rhenish" class="mw-redirect" title="Low Rhenish">Low Rhenish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorbian_languages" title="Sorbian languages">Sorbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romany_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romany language">Romany</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Frisian_language" title="North Frisian language">North Frisian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saterland_Frisian_language" title="Saterland Frisian language">Saterland Frisian</a>; they are officially protected by the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a>. The most used immigrant languages are <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish language">Kurdish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan languages">Balkan languages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>. Germans are typically multilingual: 67% of German citizens claim to be able to communicate in at least one foreign language and 27% in at least two.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages-229">[224]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Germany" title="Education in Germany">Education in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg/220px-Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg/330px-Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg/440px-Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2068" data-file-height="1680"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Heidelberg_Universit%C3%A4tsbibliothek_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a> is Germany's oldest institution of higher learning and generally counted among its most prestigious.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Responsibility for educational supervision in Germany is primarily organised within the individual <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">states</a>. Optional <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> education is provided for all children between three and six years old, after which <a href="/wiki/Schulpflicht" title="Schulpflicht">school attendance is compulsory</a> for at least nine years. Primary education usually lasts for four to six years.<sup id="cite_ref-ED_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ED-232">[227]</a></sup> Secondary schooling is divided into tracks based on whether students pursue <a href="/wiki/College-preparatory_school" title="College-preparatory school">academic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[228]</a></sup> A system of apprenticeship called <i><a href="/wiki/Dual_education_system" title="Dual education system">Duale Ausbildung</a></i> leads to a skilled qualification which is almost comparable to an academic degree. It allows students in <a href="/wiki/Vocational_training" class="mw-redirect" title="Vocational training">vocational training</a> to learn in a company as well as in a state-run trade school.<sup id="cite_ref-ED_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ED-232">[227]</a></sup> This model is well regarded and reproduced all around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[229]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Germany" title="List of universities in Germany">German universities</a> are public institutions, and students traditionally study without fee payment.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[230]</a></sup> The general requirement for university is the <i><a href="/wiki/Abitur" title="Abitur">Abitur</a></i>. According to an OECD report in 2014, Germany is the world's third leading destination for international study.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[231]</a></sup> The established universities in Germany include some of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest universities in continuous operation">oldest in the world</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_University" title="Heidelberg University">Heidelberg University</a> (established in 1386) being the oldest.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[232]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt University of Berlin</a>, founded in 1810 by the liberal educational reformer <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">Wilhelm von Humboldt</a>, became the academic <a href="/wiki/Humboldtian_model_of_higher_education" title="Humboldtian model of higher education">model for many Western universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[234]</a></sup> In the contemporary era Germany has developed eleven <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">Universities of Excellence</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Germany" title="Healthcare in Germany">Healthcare in Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG/220px-Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG/330px-Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG/440px-Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2432"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Heiligen-Geist-Hospital_in_L%C3%BCbeck.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Hospital of the Holy Spirit in <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck" title="Lübeck">Lübeck</a>, established in 1286, is a precursor to modern hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[235]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Germany's system of hospitals, called <i>Krankenhäuser</i>, dates from medieval times, and today, Germany has the world's oldest <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> system, dating from <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck#Social_legislation" title="Otto von Bismarck">Bismarck's social legislation</a> of the 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[236]</a></sup> Since the 1880s, reforms and provisions have ensured a balanced health care system. The population is covered by a health insurance plan provided by statute, with criteria allowing some groups to opt for a private health insurance contract. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, Germany's <a href="/wiki/Health_care_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care system">health care system</a> was 77% government-funded and 23% privately funded as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-health_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health-242">[237]</a></sup> In 2014, Germany spent 11.3% of its GDP on health care.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[238]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany ranked 20th in the world in 2013 in life expectancy with <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">77 years for men and 82 years for women</a>, and it had a very low <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> (4 per 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Live_birth_(human)" title="Live birth (human)">live births</a>). In 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the principal cause of death was cardiovascular disease, at 37%.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[239]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">Obesity</a> in Germany has been increasingly cited as a major health issue. A 2014 study showed that 52 percent of the adult German population was overweight or obese.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[240]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Germany" title="Culture of Germany">Culture of Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg/220px-Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg/330px-Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg/440px-Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2362" data-file-height="1575"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Striezelmarkt_2009_00950.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A typical German <i>Weihnachtsmarkt</i> (<a href="/wiki/Christmas_market" title="Christmas market">Christmas market</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Culture in German states has been shaped by major intellectual and popular currents in Europe, both religious and <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secular</a>. Historically, Germany has been called <i>Das Land der Dichter und Denker</i> ("the land of poets and thinkers"),<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[241]</a></sup> because of the major role its <a href="/wiki/German_literature" title="German literature">writers</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_philosophy" title="German philosophy">philosophers</a> have played in the development of Western thought.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[242]</a></sup> A global opinion poll for the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> revealed that Germany is recognised for having the most positive influence in the world in 2013 and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[244]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Germany is well known for such folk festival traditions as <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">Oktoberfest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weihnachten" title="Weihnachten">Christmas customs</a>, which include <a href="/wiki/Advent_wreath" title="Advent wreath">Advent wreaths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nativity_play" title="Nativity play">Christmas pageants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stollen" title="Stollen">Stollen</a> cakes, and other practices.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[245]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[246]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Germany&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> inscribed <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites_in_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites in Germany">41 properties in Germany on the World Heritage List</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[247]</a></sup> There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Germany" title="Public holidays in Germany">public holidays in Germany</a> determined by each state; 3 October has been a <a href="/wiki/National_day" title="National day">national day</a> of Germany since 1990, celebrated as the <i>Tag der Deutschen Einheit</i> (<a href="/wiki/German_Unity_Day" title="German Unity Day">German Unity Day</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[248]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Germany" title="Music of Germany">Music of Germany</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Beethoven.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Beethoven.jpg/170px-Beethoven.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Beethoven.jpg/255px-Beethoven.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Beethoven.jpg/340px-Beethoven.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1443"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Beethoven.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> (1770–1827), composer
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>German <a href="/wiki/Classical_music_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical music era">classical music</a> includes works by some of the world's most well-known composers. <a href="/wiki/Dieterich_Buxtehude" title="Dieterich Buxtehude">Dieterich Buxtehude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Frideric_Handel" title="George Frideric Handel">Georg Friedrich Händel</a> were influential composers of the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque period</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> was a crucial figure in the transition between the Classical and <a href="/wiki/Romantic_music" title="Romantic music">Romantic</a> eras. <a href="/wiki/Carl_Maria_von_Weber" title="Carl Maria von Weber">Carl Maria von Weber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felix_Mendelssohn" title="Felix Mendelssohn">Felix Mendelssohn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schumann" title="Robert Schumann">Robert Schumann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a> were significant Romantic composers. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a> was known for his operas. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a> was a leading composer of the late Romantic and early <a href="/wiki/20th-century_classical_music" title="20th-century classical music">modern</a> eras. <a href="/wiki/Karlheinz_Stockhausen" title="Karlheinz Stockhausen">Karlheinz Stockhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Rihm" title="Wolfgang Rihm">Wolfgang Rihm</a> are important composers of the 20th and early 21st centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[249]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2013, Germany was the second largest music market in Europe, and fourth largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[250]</a></sup> German popular music of the 20th and 21st centuries includes the movements of <a href="/wiki/Neue_Deutsche_Welle" title="Neue Deutsche Welle">Neue Deutsche Welle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ostrock" class="mw-redirect" title="Ostrock">Ostrock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>/<a href="/wiki/German_rock" class="mw-redirect" title="German rock">rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_punk" title="German punk">punk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volksmusik" title="Volksmusik">Volksmusik</a> (folk music), <a href="/wiki/Schlager_music" title="Schlager music">schlager pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_hip_hop" title="German hip hop">German hip hop</a>. German <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> gained global influence, with <a href="/wiki/Kraftwerk" title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangerine_Dream" title="Tangerine Dream">Tangerine Dream</a> pioneering in this genre.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[251]</a></sup> DJs and artists of the <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house music</a> scenes of Germany have become well known (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Paul_van_Dyk" title="Paul van Dyk">Paul van Dyk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felix_Jaehn" title="Felix Jaehn">Felix Jaehn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kalkbrenner" title="Paul Kalkbrenner">Paul Kalkbrenner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Schulz" title="Robin Schulz">Robin Schulz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scooter_(band)" title="Scooter (band)">Scooter</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[252]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_design">Art and design</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_art" title="German art">German art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Germany" title="Architecture of Germany">Architecture of Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_fashion" title="German fashion">German fashion</a>
      </div>
